    <a title="Nick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1121979-nick"><img alt="Nick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514584881p2/1121979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/28371010?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick" href="/user/show/1121979-nick">Nick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781427205124" href="/book/show/3424877-ender-in-exile">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1121979-nick?shelf=ficton-non-didactic">ficton-non-didactic</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28371010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16277902155313139293">Card can write fantastically in his sleep, although I kind of feel like he snored right through this one a little too much. It fills the same role in the Enderverse as <i>Back to the Future II</i>: a good story in its own right, but kind of just something to fill in the holes between his really great works. It feels like about 3 or 4 short stories that were smooshed together like play-doh.<br/><br/>Card makes Ender too much of a <a href='http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Sue' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mary Sue</a> character here. He's always right, always has a plan, and is smarter than e</span>
  <span id="freeText16277902155313139293" style="display:none">Card can write fantastically in his sleep, although I kind of feel like he snored right through this one a little too much. It fills the same role in the Enderverse as <i>Back to the Future II</i>: a good story in its own right, but kind of just something to fill in the holes between his really great works. It feels like about 3 or 4 short stories that were smooshed together like play-doh.<br /><br />Card makes Ender too much of a <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mary_Sue" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary Sue</a> character here. He's always right, always has a plan, and is smarter than everyone else. The conflicts were not at all suspenseful, and easily overcome by the protagonist. Card's expertise at characterization and dialogue save the book; I loved and cared about the characters and was entertained the whole way. I just expected more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16277902155313139293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer11528055470680644770">I'm honestly not sure this book needed to exist. While it does tie up all the dangling plotlines from the Shadow series, the book as a whole doesn't really have any driving conflict. It's more just "here's what happened to Ender in the immediate aftermath of the Bugger War."   <span id="freeText11528055470680644770" style="display:none">I'm honestly not sure this book needed to exist. While it does tie up all the dangling plotlines from the Shadow series, the book as a whole doesn't really have any driving conflict. It's more just "here's what happened to Ender in the immediate aftermath of the Bugger War." There are two seeming conflicts in the book, but they both seem manufactured, just to give Ender something to do.<br /><br />Thrilled as I am to have another Ender book, I think it would have been better if the Bean stories had just been wrapped up in a novelette, or even better, at the end of the last Shadow book.<br /><br />Perhaps the main conflict I'm missing is an internal one within Ender, where he has to confront the killer inside, but that conflict was wrapped up pretty nicely, I thought, in the actual Ender's Game sequels.<br /><br /><br /></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2385250-blake-petit?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer58500537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13722830261714003522">Continuing my chronological reread of the Ender books, I've reached this "direct" sequel to the original ENDER'S GAME. It was an enjoyable read, but as a book, it doesn't have much of an identity in and of itself. Much of it is a detailed expansion and revision of the last chapter of ENDER'S GAME. Other parts serve as an epilogue to SHADOW OF THE GIANT, picking up on a dangling plot thread remaining from Bean's series. Still more of it works to justify some of the major cultural changes in the '</span>
  <span id="freeText13722830261714003522" style="display:none">Continuing my chronological reread of the Ender books, I've reached this "direct" sequel to the original ENDER'S GAME. It was an enjoyable read, but as a book, it doesn't have much of an identity in and of itself. Much of it is a detailed expansion and revision of the last chapter of ENDER'S GAME. Other parts serve as an epilogue to SHADOW OF THE GIANT, picking up on a dangling plot thread remaining from Bean's series. Still more of it works to justify some of the major cultural changes in the 'verse between ENDER'S GAME and its original sequel, SPEAKER FOR THE DEAD. As a fan of the series as a whole and of universe-building works in general, I enjoy the book, but I feel more as though I've read a series of novellas or short stories starring the same characters and linking to larger works instead of a complete novel in and of itself. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13722830261714003522" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3022490552&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3022490552" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14650547133915116627">Orson never fails to impress, ender in exile is a very densly packed books that tries to tie as manly loose ends up from between enders game and speaker for the dead as possible while still being an interesting and coherent story. I'd say it won on all fronts, even without being flawless. <br/><br/><br/>This book reads a little like a fast forward of a much longer book, the depth of detail to the alien world and the human politics within just didn't hold up to speaker for the dead standards, it left me kinda w</span>
  <span id="freeText14650547133915116627" style="display:none">Orson never fails to impress, ender in exile is a very densly packed books that tries to tie as manly loose ends up from between enders game and speaker for the dead as possible while still being an interesting and coherent story. I'd say it won on all fronts, even without being flawless. <br /><br /><br />This book reads a little like a fast forward of a much longer book, the depth of detail to the alien world and the human politics within just didn't hold up to speaker for the dead standards, it left me kinda wishing Orson had spent less time on the ride to the planet and instead spent it on the actual planet itself. The community didnt feel as alive as previous books and the people on those planets felt a bit one dimensional. With the third planet visited seeming out of place with how little detail was given. It was more of a giant plot device incubator.<br /><br /><br />Overall very interesting story that answered alot of questions that needed answering, in a setting that would have benefitted with more screen time on a planet rather then ship.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2336100879" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2336100879" />
    <a title="Mike" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8265778-mike"><img alt="Mike" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1332129254p2/8265778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2336100879?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/8265778-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2336100879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2985023308215723849">Exile, is, in this reader's opinion, far more complete than Ender's Game. In the short span of his voyage to his second home, Ender is so much more fleshed out, more well understood. By now, Card has had several ventures into the mind of his greatest character, and IT SHOWS. While I certainly intend to read the rest of the vast Enderverse, Exile may well be the peak by which the others are, unintentionally, measured.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F+LryuQrlLHpLLdwhBnEb6t9dvvb/ID0PZEp9cggJJg58xu/qj1fCUwcYugzn6NG71ByGZoRNubczkSzcB6G8w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Xl0PtJWC9eckHKvU8XEDC6LkU+z3CxCTjy+e79VdlgdwTP/B25Q+X4EsfkxG92Qi5slXDrbmpoFucPOpbWM0bA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10980465010082297922">Orson Scott Card is the author of the novels <i>Ender's Game</i>, <i>Ender's Shadow</i>, and <i>Speaker for the Dead</i>, which are widely read by adults and younger readers, and are increasingly used in schools.<br/><br/>Besides these and other science fiction novels, Card writes contemporary fantasy (<i>Magic Street</i>, <i>Enchantment</i>, <i>Lost Boys</i>), biblical novels (<i>Stone Tables</i>, <i>Rachel and Leah</i>), the American frontier fantasy series Th</span>
  <span id="freeText10980465010082297922" style="display:none">Orson Scott Card is the author of the novels <i>Ender's Game</i>, <i>Ender's Shadow</i>, and <i>Speaker for the Dead</i>, which are widely read by adults and younger readers, and are increasingly used in schools.<br /><br />Besides these and other science fiction novels, Card writes contemporary fantasy (<i>Magic Street</i>, <i>Enchantment</i>, <i>Lost Boys</i>), biblical novels (<i>Stone Tables</i>, <i>Rachel and Leah</i>), the American frontier fantasy series The Tales of Alvin Maker (beginning with <i>Seventh Son</i>), poetry (<i>An Open Book</i>), and many plays and scripts.<br /><br />Card was born in Washington and grew up in California, Arizona, and Utah. He served a mission for the LDS Church in Brazil in the early 1970s. Besides his writing, he teaches occasional classes and workshops and directs plays. He recently began a long-term position as a professor of writing and literature at Southern Virginia University.<br /><br />Card currently lives in Greensboro, North Carolina, with his wife, Kristine Allen Card, and their youngest child, Zina Margaret.<br /><br /><i>For further details, see the author's <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orson_Scott_Card" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia</a> page.<br />For an ordered list of the author's works, see Wikipedia's <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_works_by_Orson_Scott_Card" rel="nofollow noopener">List of works by Orson Scott Card</a>.</i><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/orsonscottcard">http://us.macmillan.com/author/orsons...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10980465010082297922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
